## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science (solid mechanics / thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for thermoelastic/plastic constitutive laws where stiffness, yield stress, and hardening behavior depend on temperature.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (Hooke + thermal strain shift): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (small-strain elastic solid with coefficient of thermal expansion)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic softening with increasing temperature)
- Nonlinear elastic (Landau-type polynomial) with T-dependent coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon^3 (anharmonic elasticity; higher-order terms matter at larger strain)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit; explicit stress form for regression): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma^(c2) with sigma = f(epsilon, T) via T-dependent c0,c1 (nonlinear elastic-plastic transition; often fit with temperature-dependent parameters)
- Power-law strain hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * (epsilon + c2)^(c3) (plastic flow/hardening magnitude decreases with temperature)
- Ludwik/Hollomon-type hardening with offset strain and T dependence: sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(-c2 * T) * (epsilon + c3)^(c4) (yield/flow stress plus hardening term)
- Saturating hardening (Voce-type, smoothed in epsilon): sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) + c2 * exp(-c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-c4 * epsilon)) (hardening approaches an asymptote; all magnitudes temperature dependent)
- Smooth elastic-to-plastic transition (tanh blend): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon * (1 - tanh(c2 * (epsilon - c3))) + (c4 * exp(-c5 * T)) * tanh(c2 * (epsilon - c3)) (switches from elastic slope to plastic flow level around a yield strain)
- Yield strain shift with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) + c3 * max(epsilon - (c4 + c5 * T), 0)^(c6) (temperature-dependent elastic range followed by hardening)
- Rational saturation in strain with T-dependent scale: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon / (epsilon + c2 * exp(-c3 * T)) (stress increases with strain then saturates; temperature shifts the saturation strain)
- Logarithmic hardening with thermal scaling: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * log(c2 * (epsilon + c3)) + c4 (empirical hardening where increments diminish with strain; temperature scales strength)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of stiffness: model E(T) decreasing with T using (c0 + c1*T), exp(-c*T), or 1/(c0 + c1*T) factors multiplying epsilon.
- Thermal expansion acts like a strain offset: use (epsilon - c* (T - c0)) inside elastic terms to represent stress-free thermal strain.
- Elastic-to-plastic transition is a regime change: use smooth gates like tanh(c*(epsilon-c0)) or piecewise max(epsilon-c0,0) to represent yielding without discontinuities.
- Work hardening that saturates with strain: use 1 - exp(-c*epsilon) or epsilon/(epsilon+c0) structures (Voce-like saturation) rather than unbounded power laws.
- Temperature shifts yield/flow levels: represent yield stress or flow stress as c0 * exp(-c1*T) or (c0 - c1*T) added to (or multiplying) hardening terms.
- Nonlinear elasticity at moderate strain: include odd powers (epsilon^3, epsilon^5) with temperature-dependent coefficients to capture anharmonic stress–strain curvature.
- Strain hardening rate decreasing with strain: log(c*epsilon + c0) or sqrt(epsilon + c0) terms capture diminishing incremental strengthening.
- Coupled temperature–strain effects: prefer structures like exp(-c*T) * (epsilon + c0)^(c1) or (c0 + c1*T) * epsilon^n to reflect that temperature mainly scales strength while strain sets nonlinearity.

Now I need to check each candidate. The candidates are complex expressions involving (c+ε)⁵, rational functions in T, exponentials, sines, logs, etc. For a candidate to match, it must reduce to a polynomial in ε and T with only the terms ε², ε·T², ε·T, and ε.

If c1=0 (or c2=0), this becomes ε⁵, which introduces ε⁵ terms that cannot be canceled unless all coefficients of ε⁵ are zero. For most candidates, the (c+ε)⁵ terms appear multiplied by T² or T or divided by (T·c+c), creating coupled T-ε terms. To get the GT's simple polynomial structure, we'd need miraculous cancellations.
